I cooked them a little longer since my kids like them tender.  We served them over the Good Old Fashioned Pancakes recipe that is also on this site.  The combination made a heavenly breakfast.  We will definitely be making these on a regular basis and yes, they did remind us of the apples at Boston Market.  Thank you for sharing Jenny!

I give this one star because the butter and  sugar aren't necessary.  I use any Red apples on hand. A little water on the bottom of a pot, cut up apples, let cook til almost soft, add cinnamon: sweet & delish without butter or sugar. Can add a touch of maple syrup or honey if wanted.

I'm really tired of candied sweet potatoes and carrot souffle and I wanted something different to go with the Easter ham so I made this. Really tasty way to use up apples! My friend who owned a restaurant and was a pastry chef used to make a stuffed croissant french toast that used a carmel sauce and apples that tasted kind of like this. If you cut open a croissant part way, spread a thin layer of cream cheese and add these apples inside before gently soaking them in a french toast custard and cooking as usual in a buttered pan, you'll have something truly amazing to serve for a fancy breakfast! I will be sure to use this recipe instead from now on!

text:
I'm glad I found a base recipe for apples.  My two little girls loved me this morning when I topped their french toast with it.  As with other reviews I read, the cornstarch was a bit much and made it the consistency of honey (Good as is if you're eating the apples as a side)  Since I was using as topping I had to adjust this a bit, added another 1/2 c water and a pinch more cinnamon.  I used granny smith so it was a perfect balance of tart/sweetness.  I used the four apple and it was not enough for 4 people, next time will double the recipe.  If you are using sweeter apples then cut down on the sugar.  I peeled and then used a apple slicer and these cuts were perfect but it also took longer time for them to be cooked thoroughly maybe double the time stated.  Great recipe as an idea for starters and can be adjusted easily to taste.  Next time will be making with skin on :D

country:
None
text:
Wonderful, quick and easy recipe.  Important to note that it does call for tart apples - like Granny Smith. If you use another type of apple, such as eating apple - Red Delicious, Golden or Gala - you will not need as much sugar and they are much, much softer.  If you saute the apples too long it will turn to an applesauce consistency when finished.  If the recipe is followed exactly as written, it does actually turn out just fine. And it is so easily tweaked. :)  I thought the reviewers that remarked that it tasted like apple pie filling were "sweet" - because I don't know what else a reader would expect it to taste like. With the exception of no lemon juice, this is basically an apple pie filling recipe made on the stove top without crust. :)
 
I made one rookie mistake tho' - I wasn't paying attention during the last two minutes of cooking I left them to cook longer. Oops!  The sauce turned to caramel.  Not bad, but not what I wanted. A few tablespoons of cold water mixed in solved that in - oh, and paying attention helps too.

I loved this recipe! Yum, yum.  I did add a few things.  I used a Gala Apple, which were rather small so ended up using about 10 of them and cut them into eights.  After cutting the apples up, I added the zest of one lemon and half of a naval orange.  I added the juice of half of a lemon and half of an orange.  After added the cornstarch, brown sugar and cinnamon (I used closer to a tsp if not a little more), I also added curry power (about a tsp or more).  The dish was delicious and a favorite with the five year old.  I will definitely make it again and again.

text:
This is a recipe I have done off the top of my head and it works.  Neat to see someone has written it down.

I use a cast iron small skillet.  I use up those apples that are going bad or getting soft-but no mealy.  The mealy ones you show give to the animals outside.

I recently had only red delicious and had been disappointed since I wanted to eat them fresh but they were not juicy.  After they sat a round for a good while, I used them up.  I had able 5 read and 1 golden.  I added vinegar to the mix right away and proceeded just as this recipe says.  I cooked them in the morning as I tidied the kitchen.

Seriously takes little effort and makes the house smell good.  Plus you cleaned up all of those rejected dry apples.

My father-in-law said they were really good.  Just add that vinegar to make them sour if you have sweet apples.  And born sugar is the only way to go!

Great recipe!  Wonderful,  simple, quick and delicious.  I serve this with waffles to my vacation rental guests who always have praises.  It's better than serving  waffles with syrup.  I cook these with a mix of apples and a little less cornstarch to produce a thinner and more  fluid syrup.  I don't over cook the  apples .  Apples are soft but still firm, and not mushy.  A few added raisins raise the applause meter a notch.

text:
I've made this recipe twice. The first time something went wrong! I doubled the recipe for a Christmas brunch and added walnuts as other reviewers did. The taste was good but the color was off! Kinda gray & a little unappetizing looking. Nevertheless, people seemed to like them. I had leftovers which I was going to put into crepes the next day.  I opened the container and the color was even worse than the day before...grayish black and ugly!  I tasted them and they were still quite edible so I put them in my crepe which was good because they were covered up! I tried making the recipe again tonight, this time adding a squish of fresh lemon juice while sauteeing the apples in butter. I also omitted the walnuts. SUCCESS! They tasted great and looked amazing too!  I will definitely make them again, WITH the lemon juice! I still would like to try adding the nuts in as I really liked the crunch they gave (plus I LOVE nuts!).  Will try adding the nuts next time with the lemon juice.  Maybe will try pecans or almonds next time, thinking the walnut skins may have contributed to the grayish color?! So glad I tried them again though because I LOVE them!!

I grew up eating my Mom's southern "fried apples" using apples, butter, sugar and cinnamon.  I later made my own version using brown sugar instead of white and also adding nutmeg.  This recipe is great!  I doubled this recipe for a 3 lb. bag of apples (about 7 large apples).  I didn't double the water because I wanted to make sure the syrup was thick enough.  I also added 1 tsp. of vanilla and 1/2 teaspoon of nutmeg.  I used Empire apples and the flavor was outstanding!  I serve this as a side dish/dessert when we have pork.  I reserved some this time to serve with waffles I want to make this weekend.  This would be great with ice cream or even recipes calling for apple pie filling.

text:
Best recipe I've found for fried apples. I did scale it down to 4 servings and I think even with the scaled down water I should have cut it down even more (instead of 1/4c maybe 2T) because mine still had a lot of liquid. I added a sprinkle of salt (which could have brought more juice out of the apples making mine liquidy) and pepper when I added the brown sugar. I've found a little salt brings out the sweetness a little more and black pepper just adds a little spice that goes well with fried apples. My family loved them.

These apples are delicious.  My husband and I love them for an easy dessert or snack.  The hardest (and most time consuming part) of the recipe is the peeling, coring, and slicing of the apples (and it's only time consuming for me since I don't have a gadget that does all that for me). These turned out beautifully and exactly as I expected - the cinnamon syrup-coated apples that I know and love from some of my favorite restaurants. But I found the cooking time to be way too short, perhaps because I used Granny Smith apples - I ended up having to cook them in the syrup for at least 10 minutes, and still they weren't quite softened all the way though. I will try this recipe again with a slightly sweeter and more tender variety.

Im usually too busy to rate recipes, but for this one I actually created an account just to give this 5 stars. Too easy and very delicious, best carmelized apples Ive ever had. I halved everything since I was making it for myself as a late night snack over vanilla bean ice cream. text:
I've made this recipe many times. I started by following it as written, and it was good. My plan was to add a small helping to a bowl of oatmeal for breakfast, which is a much tastier and healthier option than a package of instant apple cinnamon oatmeal.
My changes were to add between 1/8-1/4 of a teaspoon of both nutmeg and clove to the cinnamon and brown sugar mix. It adds so much more flavour.
Add more cornstarch if you want it a little thicker, less if you want more of a thin sauce.

MMMM! This was a great way to use a bag of apples that was slowly finding its way to the back of the fridge in the "Eh, no" area. text:
I tried this for our Christmas ham.  I don't like Granny Smith apples, so I used Fuji and Red Delicious.  I thought it was going to be too sweet, but it wasn't. I actually could've stood it a little sweeter, but everyone loved it, said it was perfect.  I added a little nutmeg, but otherwise followed the recipe exactly.  I cooked the apples a little longer to be soft, and got rave reviews.  This was the prefect complimnet dish.  Will make again for pork chops! I read the other reviews and started out using half the cornstarch, but end up using the amount the recipe called for to get the right thickness.  I also doubled the recipe for 13 people.

text:
WOW! This was great with a few tweeks.  I have lots of pears and my husband and I were getting tired of eating them plain.  I used 5 pears and reduced the butter to 2 TBSP and the sugar to 3 TBSP as one reviewer said the butter and sugar didn't add anything to it and I think that idea was right on.  Next time I would omit the butter and add 2TBSP of the sugar.

I reduced the water to 1/3 c because the pears were juicy. I also added 1/4 tsp of nutmeg and 1/8 tsp of ginger and this really improved the spice balance.

I plan to make again using apples with spices and water amount as is, no butter and 3 TBSP of sugar.

text:
Okay, I'm posting here because of my troubles with finally getting around to this recipe.

I've made apples this way before, and they turned out good. But I usually never have the ingredients on hand at my house. So here's to all the people with the same predicament, from a freshman.....

If you dont have any spices on hand, I use a simple recipe that creates decadent, gorgeous soft apples.

You will need: Apples (cored and cut up), butter (to cover a pan), sugar, and a squeezable lemon juice.

Cut the apples. Put a round skillet over low heat. Butter it when hot. Throw the apples in and saute. Occasionally sift white sugar onto the apples evenly with a spoon, saute more, and squeeze a hint of lemon juice on them. Theyre ready when a fork doesnt push through them, but makes a dent. Delicious.

text:
Wonderful recipe that does remind me of the Boston Market apples! My ingredient modifications included dissolving cornstarch in apple cider instead of water, increasing the amount of cinnamon, and adding a touch of allspice and nutmeg. I also threw a few peach slices in the pot and it's a delicious addition; I'm secretly hoping my husband doesn't want any (he doesn't like apples) so I can go finish the pot. The next time I make this, I will decrease the cornstarch (as I had to add water while it was cooking), not use as much cinnamon and stick to the recipe, and increase the nutmeg (because I love it). I cooked on medium-low because I only used one apple and a few peach slices---even if I make the original 8 serving recipe, I would still recommend low heat and more time. Finally, because I didn't have tart apples, I splashed some lemon juice onto the apple slices, which also preventing browning, as I was cooking other things and needed to let them sit for a little. Thanks again for a fab recipe---it's a keeper! Delicious w/my breakfast, which included scrambled eggs w/beef smoked sausage.

My grandmother used to make "fried apples" as part of her huge buffet breakfasts everytime I went to visit her in KY (such a fond memory) and they were the best thing I had ever eaten. Until now I had no idea how to offer this to my family short of opening a can of pie filling and throwing in a skillet! text:
I thought this tasted very good. A few tips, however: 1) I don't think the cornstarch is necessary. 2) I cut the recipe down to 2 servings because I only have myself and my husband to feed and I was using it as a waffle topping because I was out of syrup. I used 1 apple (red delicious sliced thicker and not sauted as long worked wonderfully) but the sauce was pretty much non-existant. it covered the apples but there wasn't anything left so I concocted the sauce without the apples to have more syrup. worked well. 3) I tried one reviewer's idea and added nutmeg and vanilla. The vanilla was a good addition but I didn't really care for the nutmeg. It didn't ruin the recipe, but it didn't add anything to it either and it smelled funny. I think the recipe is great tasting as is but if you decrease the number of apples, you still need to keep the same amount of sauce or you just have flavored apples, no sauce. remember, if you use a softer apple, just decrease the sautee time to a minute or two instead of 6 minutes. You just have to get them warm because they're already soft. PS. Anyone who thought this recipe was disgusting must have done something wrong. I don't think I would eat it by itself, though, use as a topping for something. But it is definately NOT disgusting. My husband gave it five stars, too.

These apples were amazing!  I used the same variety of apples that I use in apple pie (Granny Smith, McIntosh, and Fuji).  I used my apple peeler/slicer to speed the prep. process. Also added a pinch of nutmeg.  Wonderful topping for pancakes!
